<div id="review_1349381375" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1349381375" />
    <a title="Liam (Hey Ashers!)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32591937-liam-hey-ashers"><img alt="Liam (Hey Ashers!)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459356799p2/32591937.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1349381375?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liam (Hey Ashers!)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liam (Hey Ashers!)" href="/user/show/32591937-liam-hey-ashers">Liam (Hey Ashers!)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32591937-liam-hey-ashers?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32591937-liam-hey-ashers?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1349381375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10760569997985968052"><i>This is a review originally posted on <a href='http://www.heyashers.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hey Ashers!</a></i><br/><br/><i>Spoiler Rating: Moderate</i><br/><br/>Dear Lizzy,<br/><br/>I've lugged veritable carloads of novels home from Half Price Books, most of which have subsequently been lugged <i>back</i> to Half Price Books for reselling. <i>The Darkangel</i> came home with me, oh, five or six years ago, and has sat brooding on my shelf until a few days ago, when I finally decided, <i>Eh, it's time</i>.<br/><br/>Ignoring the weirdness of "astounding youth" (what is he, a toddler?) and "beautiful terror" (I don't even kno</span>
  <span id="freeText10760569997985968052" style="display:none"><i>This is a review originally posted on <a href="http://www.heyashers.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Hey Ashers!</a></i><br><br><i>Spoiler Rating: Moderate</i><br><br>Dear Lizzy,<br><br>I've lugged veritable carloads of novels home from Half Price Books, most of which have subsequently been lugged <i>back</i> to Half Price Books for reselling. <i>The Darkangel</i> came home with me, oh, five or six years ago, and has sat brooding on my shelf until a few days ago, when I finally decided, <i>Eh, it's time</i>.<br><br>Ignoring the weirdness of "astounding youth" (what is he, a toddler?) and "beautiful terror" (I don't even know), the synopsis sounds promising! But <i>The Darkangel</i> was not quite what I thought it was going to be.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457049529i/18313725.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Awesome: The Setting</b><br><br>The moon. This book takes place on the moon.<br><br>Something over a thousand years in the future, humans have terraformed the moon and developed (what's presumably) a mutated/modified human species that can survive much harsher conditions—so when the the artificial atmosphere begins to thin, the humans' domed cities start failing, and war (or disease, or something) calls the humans back to Earth, the mutated/modified humans continue to thrive on the moon.<br><br>By the time the story begins, most of the atmosphere has gone, there is almost no surface water available, and the ancient humans who created them are mostly-forgotten religious-ish figures.<br><br>Enter Aeriel, a slave girl, and Eoduin, her mistress, climbing into the high peaks to pick rare flowers:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456376878i/18225488._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The desolate landscape, the black sky and white sun, the long day and long night (the sun is up for [I'm guessing; it's never counted out] about 14 earth-days, and down for as long; a single day/night cycle is referred to as a day-month), the danger of cold and airlessness all combine to make a superb backdrop for a slightly creepy fairy tale—which <i>The Darkangel</i> is, in essence.<br><br>And oh, man, I can't tell you how much I love that the lack of atmosphere on the highest peaks mutes voices to the point that even screams are only slight sounds. That is terrifying and <i>so good</i>.<br><br><b>Not Really Romance</b><br><br>All that said, I greatly enjoyed the fact that this wasn't really a romance. I don't want to go into spoilers, but this is a very Beauty and the Beast type story, but not a romance. (Aeriel is too busy pursuing her goal to be romanced, and the darkangel is the opposite of a romantic figure anyway.)<br><br>I understand that their relationship does get romantic over the course of the rest of the trilogy, however—and I find this squicky due to their age difference. Aeriel is prepubescent at the start of this story, entering puberty a few months after she's kidnapped. Obviously I have no idea how these Moon humans mature compared to Earth humans, but I was gauging her age around twelve or thirteen (though she does sometimes sound older). The darkangel, meanwhile, is thirty.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457049529i/18313726.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Confusing: The Intended Audience</b><br><br><i>The Darkangel</i> is published under the teens division of Little Brown, which—coupled with the whole Sexy Vampire With Multiple Brides thing—led me to assume this was a book for teens. If it is, it has a <i>very</i> low opinion teens' intelligence.<br><br>For example: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[there's a prophesy in the form of a clumsy poem, and the meaning of a key line is <i>blazingly</i> obvious, but Aeriel can't figure it out—and (worse!) even when another character sits her down and spells the meaning out, she doesn't believe/understand it. She's a sobbing mess, thinking everything's ruined when it <i>clearly </i>isn't, and I just can't believe how dumb she is. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The story also skimmed over how Aeriel's experiences changed/affected her, and glossed through the certain stages of Aeriel's adventure much like a story for children: "After a day of walking, the lost duckling found a warren of rabbits, who took him in and presented him with a bed of downy fur and feasts of carrots and celery—but the duckling slept poorly underground and didn't like the taste of carrots and celery, so after a week of politely picking at his plate, he bid his farewells and continued on his way." What did the duckling learn while with the rabbits? How did his time spent with them affect his perspective on life/his adventure/his self?<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Aeriel spends several months with a certain group of people, but those months last just a few pages, and by the time she leaves them she's gained only a weapon. She doesn't form any real relationships with the people; she doesn't learn anything about herself or life or whatever; she rarely and barely thinks of her time with these people after she's left them.<br><br>I certainly don't want to bloat her journey with unnecessary stuff, but <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Aeriel seemed too little changed/affected by her experiences. It's my opinion that teens (should) expect and (definitely) deserve more than that.<br><br><b>Problematic: Beauty, Goodness, and Race</b><br><br>There's an interesting but problematic relationship between beauty, goodness, and paleness in this book.<br><br>It first appears on page two, when Aeriel is wistfully admiring Eoduin:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456376878i/18225489._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's expanded upon when Aeriel goes to meet the darkangel, intent on killing him for having kidnapped Eoduin:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456376878i/18225490._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(Note that his features, his body are not described—only the colors of him. We are constantly reminded of his beautiful paleness, and how captivated Aeriel is by him.)<br><br>It's reinforced by the darkangel's repeated comments on her ugly darkness:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456376878i/18225491._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456376878i/18225492._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And over time, the dark and ugly Aeriel changes:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456376878i/18225493._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The sun has bleached her darkness to beautiful lightness; she is now, the darkangel decides, prettier than Eoduin, whose hair was too dark. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>It's not necessarily the pale-is-more-beautiful-than-dark thing I have an issue with (though I'd really prefer more diversity, obviously; let's have darker-is-more-beautiful books, and [though less likely] color-doesn't-play-a-role-in-cultural-standards-of-beauty books, please and thanks). What makes squirm in my chair is that Aeriel herself (and the story itself) equates beauty with goodness:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456376878i/18225494._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That whole "spark of goodness" that the synopsis claims Aeriel sees in the darkangel? I never saw it. He's straight-up vicious and cruel, and several other things besides. We're just told that his beauty is evidence of his lingering goodness, and that when that goodness dies, so will his beauty. But he is also beautiful <i>because</i> he is pale. Goodness = beauty = pale. You can see the problem with this.<br><br>Fortunately, the book doesn't strictly believe its own equation. The world is populated by dark-colored people who are lovely and good. For example:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456376878i/18225495._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There's another example I'd like to give to prove that this book isn't grossly pro-pale/anti-dark, but it goes too far into spoiler territory. Trust me when I say that the equation is fairly well dismissed by the end of the novel, though.<br><br>Nonetheless, this issue makes me squirm. I wish the equation hadn't been used at all; I wish he had shown true sparks of goodness, and that beauty wasn't used as its stand-in.<br><br>(Ugh, okay. He has a screaming nightmare once, but I need a lot more than just evidence that he can feel fear. Fear doesn't equal goodness any more than beauty does. This guy <i>tortures animals</i>, for heaven's sake. It'll take a pretty significant spark to make me believe there's goodness buried in there.)<br><br><b>Disappointing: Emotional Resonance</b><br><br>I never felt much of an emotional connection with Aeriel, perhaps in part because her own emotions were fairly steady and muted. Within minutes of being kidnapped and taken to the darkangel's castle, Aeriel's initial terror has subsided:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456376878i/18225496._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She feels revulsion and fear when she meets the other denizens of the darkangel's castle, but those feelings are also swift to fade. When she faces mortal danger, she just...faces mortal danger and moves on.<br><br>Really, the one scene that dragged real emotion out of me was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the death of a horse-creature, and that only because it reminded me too strongly of watching some of our horses be put down. I was seeing Stormy fall, and his legs kicking, and Mom shading his open eye from the sun while he died, and I had to put the book down and take a lot of very deep breaths. (I'm taking deep breaths now.) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And I lied: the other scene that got to me was the whole torturing animals bit. Thank goodness <i>that</i> only lasted a page or two.<br><br>In any case, this is a story that should keep me white-knuckled and flinching and breathless, and it didn't quite manage that. I was reading to finish the book, not because I was emotionally <i>compelled</i> to read.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457049529i/18313727.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So why does it warrant two stars? Despite its (significant) flaws, this story has the potential to be really great. I was editing and plot-tweaking and rewriting (mentally, anyway) as I was reading, and enjoyed that process. I'm giving it two stars kind of in recognition of what it <i>could </i>be.<br><br>All told, this isn't a <i>bad</i> story. The setting is neat, there were some great descriptions of some pretty horrifying things, and I really liked the fresh take on the vampire/angel mythology. (These vampires are not made by being bitten/fed blood by other vampires.) It's not something I'll reread, though, and I'd hesitate to recommend it to anyone over the age of twelve (and even then, there are better books out there).<br><br>But, hey, this means another book to return to Half Price! I'm trying <i>so hard </i>not to buy more until there's space for them to fit neatly on my shelves. You'd be proud.<br><br>Love,<br><br>Liam</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="Wren " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11442507-wren"><img alt="Wren " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443235719p2/11442507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/895465674?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wren " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wren " href="/user/show/11442507-wren">Wren </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316067232" href="/book/show/180412.The_Darkangel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=unique-books">unique-books</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=exciting">exciting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=theme-kidnapped">theme-kidnapped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=young-adult-general">young-adult-general</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=amazing-storyline">amazing-storyline</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=theme-magic">theme-magic</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer895465674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2688255660225734931">Aeriel and her mistress, Eoduin, are out one day, away from their village, when the Darkangel kidnaps Eoduin to be his bride. Aeriel hopes to avenge her mistress by killing the vampyre, but she is kidnapped as well, to be his servant.<br/><br/>The Darkangel's castle is dark and depressing, guarded by menacing, chained gargoyles. Aeriel is tasked with tending to the vampyres's thirteen wives, who have now become hideous, soulless wraiths. <br/><br/>The wraiths urge her to kill the vampyre before he chooses a fourtee</span>
  <span id="freeText2688255660225734931" style="display:none">Aeriel and her mistress, Eoduin, are out one day, away from their village, when the Darkangel kidnaps Eoduin to be his bride. Aeriel hopes to avenge her mistress by killing the vampyre, but she is kidnapped as well, to be his servant.<br /><br />The Darkangel's castle is dark and depressing, guarded by menacing, chained gargoyles. Aeriel is tasked with tending to the vampyres's thirteen wives, who have now become hideous, soulless wraiths. <br /><br />The wraiths urge her to kill the vampyre before he chooses a fourteenth and final bride and the magical duarough, living in the caves beneath the castle, helps her devise a plan to lead to his undoing. But will Aeriel have the ruthlessness to truly end the Darkangel's existence? Or will her compassion motivate her to find another way to defeat his evil side? <br /><br />The first book in this trilogy by Meredith Ann Pierce was captivating, magical, and emotional. Despite some wordy descriptions and occasionally confusing dialogue, I was sucked into the story from the first chapter. <br /><br />I consider this novel to be fantasy, horror, and adventure, a combination of sub-genres I have never come across in the general young adult genre before. It included everything from winged vampires to living water to water witches to talking animals, and it took place in what appeared to be another planet or world. The horror aspect was fulfilled through the wraiths' appearances and over-all condition, along with the vampyre's gothic castle, his unpredictable temper and grisly past times, and the dark tales Aeriel tells to the inhabitants of the castle. As for the adventure, Aeriel's quest to obtain the materials necessary to kill the vampyre is an adventure both excitingly dangerous and breathtakingly beautiful.<br /><br />I felt like this book was kind of like a retelling of Beauty and the Beast. We have the woman kidnapped and brought to a beast's castle, the cast of unique and/or transformed inhabitants, and the incident of the captive running away and later returning, her compassion for her captor overcoming her fear. For this reason, I recommend this book to fans of fairy-tale retellings. <br /><br />I also recommend this book to fans of fantasy, horror, and adventure stories, and to adults and teens alike looking for a romance-free novel with paranormal themes.<br /><br />This review can also be found at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogspot.ca/2015/03/the-darkangel-by-meredith-ann-pierce.html">http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogs...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2688255660225734931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_144901739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144901739" />
    <a title="VampireNovelFan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4897902-vampirenovelfan"><img alt="VampireNovelFan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296445543p2/4897902.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144901739?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="VampireNovelFan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="VampireNovelFan" href="/user/show/4897902-vampirenovelfan">VampireNovelFan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316067232" href="/book/show/180412.The_Darkangel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144901739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2918806763178902358">This series was one of my favorites as a teen. Book 1 of the Dark Angel trilogy introduces us to Aeriel, a slave who ends up following her lifelong friend after she was captured by a Darkangel. His goal is to take 14 wives as sacrifices so that he may become a full fledged vampire. Aeriel's friend, Euodine, is to be his 13th wife. <br/><br/>Aeriel plots to be captured as well, the Darkangel deciding to take her so as to serve his wives. Upon meeting the Darkangel, she is stricken by his beauty. While he i</span>
  <span id="freeText2918806763178902358" style="display:none">This series was one of my favorites as a teen. Book 1 of the Dark Angel trilogy introduces us to Aeriel, a slave who ends up following her lifelong friend after she was captured by a Darkangel. His goal is to take 14 wives as sacrifices so that he may become a full fledged vampire. Aeriel's friend, Euodine, is to be his 13th wife. <br /><br />Aeriel plots to be captured as well, the Darkangel deciding to take her so as to serve his wives. Upon meeting the Darkangel, she is stricken by his beauty. While he is undoubtedly evil, she sees something deeper within him that makes her want to save him.<br /><br />This is not your typical romance, and really quite a bit of the story is centered around general fantasy lore and mystery. The Darkangel does not find Aeriel physically attractive, outright calling her too ugly to be one of his brides. That to me already sets up a very interesting dynamic that I enjoyed seeing played out in this book. If he is to fall for her, it would be for something deeper than her outer beauty to him. <br /><br />The writing style, while created for young adult, would translate well for general adult readers as well. The story truly made an impression on me and to this day, I think back to amazing scenes. I love the complexity of the Darkangel as a character and I think other readers would, too. <br /><br />*Review also posted to <a href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R1UOJXGBLKHXSF/ref=cm_cr_rdp_perm" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2918806763178902358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/7550098?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer7550098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11684221496279847256">Read this when I was still in high school ... happened to find it walking through the book aisle in Walgreens and wasn't all that sure I'd like it, but immediately fell in love with it and with Pierce's storytelling and forshadowing. About two years later I was walking through the same store and found the second book in the trilogy, A Gathering of Gargoyles, and was downright jumping for joy. Devoured the book that night and was even more enthusiastic to read the continuation of this story in th</span>
  <span id="freeText11684221496279847256" style="display:none">Read this when I was still in high school ... happened to find it walking through the book aisle in Walgreens and wasn't all that sure I'd like it, but immediately fell in love with it and with Pierce's storytelling and forshadowing. About two years later I was walking through the same store and found the second book in the trilogy, A Gathering of Gargoyles, and was downright jumping for joy. Devoured the book that night and was even more enthusiastic to read the continuation of this story in the third book. Unfortunately, I didn't find the third book until about 10 years after I found the first. But always looked for it in bookstores and libraries, until one day there it was. Can't say I enjoyed the third book as much as I did the first two. Felt kind of let down, but in the end it was a decent enough story. Glad to have read it and glad to have an ending to a beautiful story. That the ending wasn't what I had hoped for isn't utterly disappointing. Rather, it's just the way it came out. Hopefully, you'll enjoy it. I recommend it to anyone who enjoys stories of exploration, adventure, overcoming adversity and self-reliance ... oh yeah, and love.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ithlilian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ithlilian" href="/user/show/4793655-ithlilian">Ithlilian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4793655-ithlilian?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140059459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6036252157741459868">This book reminded me a bit of the Narnia books for some reason. Possibly due to the talking lion and the friendly gnome creature that tells stories to the main character. It also reminds me a bit of Lord of the Rings in the sense that some poem/saying is strewn throughout the entire novel. The story was interesting enough, though when you pull it all together it could be summarized in a sentence or two. Also, the ending is a bit of a surprise. One second you are engrossed in the book, and the n</span>
  <span id="freeText6036252157741459868" style="display:none">This book reminded me a bit of the Narnia books for some reason. Possibly due to the talking lion and the friendly gnome creature that tells stories to the main character. It also reminds me a bit of Lord of the Rings in the sense that some poem/saying is strewn throughout the entire novel. The story was interesting enough, though when you pull it all together it could be summarized in a sentence or two. Also, the ending is a bit of a surprise. One second you are engrossed in the book, and the next page it is over, finished, end of story.<br /><br />Usually, the amount of detail and description in this book would have bored me, but The Darkangel makes you feel like you are there, living with the characters. I cared what the honey flowers in the beginning of the book looked and tasted like, and even though there wasn't action at every turn of the page, I was entertained. The whole thing felt like a long short story, if that makes any sense. I felt like it was a story being told from a wise elder, or a grandmother figure, and I was just along for the ride. Overall, a pretty enjoyable story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6036252157741459868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The sci-fi aspect (setting) is integrated with subtlety as opposed to tacked on, and the main character is neither cowering or feisty. She is a fairytale heroine.   <span id="freeText1236807269808532250" style="display:none">This is a book that sounds cliche and unappealing when you try to describe it's subject or plot. The reality of it is graceful and has the quality of a fairytale however. The sci-fi aspect (setting) is integrated with subtlety as opposed to tacked on, and the main character is neither cowering or feisty. She is a fairytale heroine. She does what must be done, treats others with care and and respect, but is secondary to the story and her destiny, more than looming larger than life. It's a surprisingly quiet story, but one with great dignity and charm.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11648664527113993206">Maybe I should give it 3 stars - I liked the idea and the writing wasn't bad. <br/><br/>I thought the world building was pretty poor, though.   <span id="freeText11648664527113993206" style="display:none">Maybe I should give it 3 stars - I liked the idea and the writing wasn't bad. <br /><br />I thought the world building was pretty poor, though. I struggled to understand the concepts of the magical protectors and even of time. What was a day-month? I honestly didn't get that. <i>Was</i> it a month or not? <br /><br />Worst of all were the characters for me. No personality whatsoever and I was pretty disappointed with Aeriel's sole focus on the darkangel's beauty. I can't say that I saw the 'spark of goodness' in him mentioned in the blurb and there is nothing more to him. <br /><br />Oh, and how Aeriel didn't realise who he was straight away after her story-telling, I have no idea.<br /><br />2.5 stars overall and not much interest in continuing the series, sadly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11648664527113993206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_27387449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27387449" />
    <a title="Melissa McShane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1329059-melissa-mcshane"><img alt="Melissa McShane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216147749p2/1329059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27387449?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa McShane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa McShane" href="/user/show/1329059-melissa-mcshane">Melissa McShane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780812549003" href="/book/show/1162013.The_Darkangel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27387449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11727056591769041156">I absolutely loved this book as a teen. I was crushed to realize I didn't love it as an adult.<br/><br/>I'm still captivated by the world Pierce creates: Earth's moon, altered to support life that is itself genetically engineered to live there, its natural rotation providing 14-Earth Day "nights" and "days," the atmosphere thin enough to barely refract light. Aeriel, a slave in the local ruler's household, is devoted to her young mistress Eoduin, and when Eoduin is captured by an icarus--a vampiric winged</span>
  <span id="freeText11727056591769041156" style="display:none">I absolutely loved this book as a teen. I was crushed to realize I didn't love it as an adult.<br /><br />I'm still captivated by the world Pierce creates: Earth's moon, altered to support life that is itself genetically engineered to live there, its natural rotation providing 14-Earth Day "nights" and "days," the atmosphere thin enough to barely refract light. Aeriel, a slave in the local ruler's household, is devoted to her young mistress Eoduin, and when Eoduin is captured by an icarus--a vampiric winged creature--Aeriel vows to find her and bring her back. She's also captured and brought to the icarus's castle to care for his thirteen wives, all of them (including Eoduin) withered and mostly dead because the icarus has taken their souls. He's collecting them to take to his "mother" in the Wastes, and in a year, when he takes his fourteenth, she will make him a true vampyre. (I did not make up that spelling.)<br /><br />There's just such wonderful imagery in this story, like the caverns underground where Aeriel's companion the duarough lives. Or the golden drop spindle that spins thread out of Aeriel's emotions--hate, fear, love all producing different threads. Or Aeriel's encounter with the banished guardian of her country. It's beautifully evocative.<br /><br />What it cannot do is obscure the fact that the icarus is soulless, cruel, selfish, violent, and a murderer, and that Aeriel's growing attraction to him despite her knowing all of this is perverse. When the duarough calls her on it the first time, she says that she is drawn to the icarus because he is beautiful (of course he is, it's a vampire story, but at least Pierce has the good sense to also make him inhuman and thus a little repellent) and, more disturbingly, that anyone that beautiful cannot be completely evil.<br /><br />Excuse me?<br /><br />In context, what Aeriel is really saying is that she feels pity for the icarus, who was once a human kidnapped and transformed by the Witch of the Wastes. As the plot progresses, we see the icarus being affected by Aeriel's presence and her actions, but he doesn't become a better person. Surprisingly, this works to show Aeriel's point: you can feel pity for someone without approving of their behavior. And it would have been a good story, if it hadn't gotten tangled up in the romantic-love version of the plot. There's no reason for Aeriel to fall in love with the icarus. He does nothing to make himself emotionally appealing or to repudiate his violent, sociopathic behavior. The only thing he has going for him is that he's gorgeous and has a tortured past...wait, I take it back, that's *exactly* why she should fall in love with him.<br /><br />Seriously, this is not a convincing love story, but since it's part of the story, the book is not a convincing story about redemption either. It's just muddled. I wish it had gone one way or the other, or even that Aeriel had seen the icarus as evil, killed him, and then had to deal with the fallout. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This assumes that in killing the icarus, she actually freed Irrylath from the Witch's spell. On the other hand, since Irrylath clearly doesn't remember anything after being kidnapped when he was six, he's still got the mind of a child, and if they're married, that's just ooky. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I will always love this book for what it does brilliantly, but now my feelings about it are deeply conflicted.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11727056591769041156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_251351325" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/251351325" />
    <a title="Fey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2056399-fey"><img alt="Fey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333291219p2/2056399.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/251351325?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fey" href="/user/show/2056399-fey">Fey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316067232" href="/book/show/180412.The_Darkangel">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">children, adults, fantasy and fairy-tale lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=on-my-bookshelf">on-my-bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=second-hand">second-hand</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=2012-must-read">2012-must-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=fluff-free">fluff-free</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251351325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13051595218965730488">Aeriel is a young slave-girl, who serves Eoduin, the pretty daughter of the town syndic. Being only 2 years younger than Eoduin makes them close friends as well as mistress and slave, and Aeriel very much looks up to the older girl. <br/><br/>One day Aeriel and Eoduin are on high on the mountains outside of town, picking flower nectar for a traditional drink for a wedding thats soon to be held in town. But while they are separately wandering on the mountain, a darkangel flies down - a luminous pale being </span>
  <span id="freeText13051595218965730488" style="display:none">Aeriel is a young slave-girl, who serves Eoduin, the pretty daughter of the town syndic. Being only 2 years younger than Eoduin makes them close friends as well as mistress and slave, and Aeriel very much looks up to the older girl. <br /><br />One day Aeriel and Eoduin are on high on the mountains outside of town, picking flower nectar for a traditional drink for a wedding thats soon to be held in town. But while they are separately wandering on the mountain, a darkangel flies down - a luminous pale being with huge black wings - and captures Eoduin. The darkangel is a considered a mythical being, only talked about in scary stories told to young children, so when Aeriel returns to the village no one believes her tale, and some even believe that she has killed Eoduin. <br /><br />With no one believing her, Aeriel decides to take it upon herself to return to the top of the mountain, wait for the darkangel, and kill him. But when the darkangel appears again, she is bewitched by his beauty and unable to carry out the deed. And so the darkangel carries her off to his huge abandoned castle, where she is to serve his 13 wives, who are all now emaciated soulless wraiths, (including the latest who is of course Aeriel's friend Eoduin). Aeriel's learns that when the darkangel takes his 14th wife, a year from now, he will finally have enough souls to become a full vampyre. And at that point he will join his 6 other vampyre brothers and they would conquer and divide the entire world between them. Aeriel knows she could be the only one who can kill the vampyre before he takes his 14th wife, if only she can bring herself to do it.<br /><br />This is novel is an amazing blend of fantasy, fairy-tale and science fiction, in a very similar style and theme to the Narnia books. I thought it was absolutely beautiful, and I wish I had discovered it when I was still a kid, it's just the sort of thing I would have fallen in love with back then.<br /><br />Aeriel is a lovely main character, she has a lot of complexity of emotion, which it great for a kids book. She is strong and courageous under pressure, and she perserveres in such daunting situations, but without ever becoming overly sure of herself. I also love how she stands up to the darkangel, even tho she is by turns enraptured and then afraid of him. <br /><br />Although, like other reviewers, I wish there had been a greater depth to her relationship with him, as she never seems truly sure of her feelings towards him, and being that it's her feelings towards him that gives rise to the entire dilemma of whether to save or kill him - and save or doom the world.. well it perhaps requires a little more certainty in her emotions to make it a meaningful conflict and resolution.<br /><br />I really think the book could have done with a glossary of terms, as there are several things that confused me right up until the end, such as the term 'day-month', which I now gather to mean that it takes a month for the day/night cycle (2 weeks night, two weeks daylight), but I'm still not entirely sure. But this is only a minor quibble compared to how much I really enjoyed the book, so hopefully it won't put off anyone else.<br /><br />Would recommend this book for both children and adults aged 10 to 100+ and anyone with a love for fantasy and fairytales. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13051595218965730488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78419405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78419405" />
    <a title="Lara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/309689-lara"><img alt="Lara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465346130p2/309689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78419405?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lara" href="/user/show/309689-lara">Lara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780001841499" href="/book/show/1162016.The_Darkangel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/309689-lara?shelf=libraried">libraried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/309689-lara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/309689-lara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/309689-lara?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78419405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3860202178717251220">Well, this WAS inventive and beautiful, but...I guess I was just hoping for something more than that. <br/><br/>There's so little character development that it was impossible for me to feel any attachment to anybody, and I kept waiting around wondering when the darkangel's supposed deep-down goodness would manifest itself, but it never really did, until his circumstances drastically changed at the very end. I never quite figured out how Aeriel came to love him--it seemed that they spent very little actual</span>
  <span id="freeText3860202178717251220" style="display:none">Well, this WAS inventive and beautiful, but...I guess I was just hoping for something more than that. <br /><br />There's so little character development that it was impossible for me to feel any attachment to anybody, and I kept waiting around wondering when the darkangel's supposed deep-down goodness would manifest itself, but it never really did, until his circumstances drastically changed at the very end. I never quite figured out how Aeriel came to love him--it seemed that they spent very little actual time together, and most of that time he was busy threatening her or chasing her around trying to kill her. Her thought process pretty much seemed to be, "He's beautiful! But he's evil! But he's so beautiful! But he wants to kill me! But he's really, really beautiful!" I just didn't get it is all. <br /><br />There were several things I really loved about the book though--the wraithes, and the fourteen vials containing their souls that the darkangel wore around his neck, and I very much liked the parts of the story that took place in the desert, and the symbolism of the trading of hearts. <br /><br />I feel like this book could have been AMAZING but, mainly because of the poor character development, it just fell a little flat for me. I still may read the second book in the trilogy, but I certainly don't feel any real compulsion to do so. Maybe I just came to this story too late in life...</span>
  <a data-text-id="3860202178717251220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284114756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16764948149077377232">I had an enjoyable afteroon reading this one at the beach. <br/>Aeriel is a slave/companion of a girl named Euodin. She's been bullied into helping her gather flowers for a wedding on the mountains. Eeodin doesn't take Aeriels concerns or the tales about a vampyre who kidnaps pretty girls seriously.<br/>When she's taken Aeriel is blamed and is told she'll be going back to the slave markets in a month.<br/>Seeing that no one else in the village is going to avenge her mistress she decides to kill the vampyre her</span>
  <span id="freeText16764948149077377232" style="display:none">I had an enjoyable afteroon reading this one at the beach. <br />Aeriel is a slave/companion of a girl named Euodin. She's been bullied into helping her gather flowers for a wedding on the mountains. Eeodin doesn't take Aeriels concerns or the tales about a vampyre who kidnaps pretty girls seriously.<br />When she's taken Aeriel is blamed and is told she'll be going back to the slave markets in a month.<br />Seeing that no one else in the village is going to avenge her mistress she decides to kill the vampyre herself.<br />I knew this was a book for me when the vampyre laughed in her face when she thinks she's being taken for a bride. She is too ugly for someone as hot as him!<br />Aeriel is to be a servant for his thirteen wives who have become wraiths. The vampyre has sucked out their souls on his wedding night every year.<br />This was a very entertaining tale that has a clever spin on the vampire bad boy. Will she be able to "change" him?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16764948149077377232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kTt4afhXE+gwPg+Z0JVCJEkekGHjeeu2yCwW+GdLsyigIClS2sqWXn8p5AhozORzchHHrhlIdETiQ5wOeodi0w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mM6hx3Ah7PCWAnl864I8uJN4T9y0VKKecPIrukQC4lep1fD8UrxpRtkVku1T25rvqHcYE05lPWxanaFMWc4zrA==')})
  }

It has been so long.\n\nOne scent of her blood essence would surely send me over the edge, giving the awakened one the upper hand as he urged me to side with him. I braced myself for the battle against the leech within me and begged him to leave me in peace.\n\nI held my breath and didn’t move a muscle, for fear the beast might interpret any sudden movement as permission to strike. When I could no longer hold my breath, I exhaled, then inhaled slowly and shallowly. I waited for her fragrance to signal my defeat, giving the leech the permission to strike.\n\nI readied myself to charge against this inner beast when her aromatic essence penetrated my line of defense. When her aroma registered in my brain, I waited to see what my level of temptation would be. The beast received the verdict first and my battle was won as he retreated.\nI was intrigued by Chansey’s unexpected essence. It wasn’t unappealing, yet not enticing either. It was neutral and I was spellbound.\n\nShe lifted her head from my chest and leaned back to see my face. “I don’t know what to say or how to thank you.”\n\nShe raised up onto her tiptoes and planted a kiss on my cheek before she released her hold of me. I reluctantly released my hold, as well, but I wasn’t finished exploring this. I wanted more, I needed more.\n\nWe both knew we had just shared a significant moment, although neither of us voiced it.\n“I’m sure you’re exhausted. You should get a good night’s rest,” I said, verbally encouraging her to go to bed, but inside begging her stay.\n\nI regretfully watched her walk up the steps to the backdoor. Before entering, she turned and said, “Thank you again, Curry. You’re a real life saver.”\n\nThe paradox of her words brought a smile to my face. She saw a life saver in a skilled killer and I was tantalized by the mystery of her. The leech inside me came out to find prey, but found none in this enigmatic girl. The proximity of her essence didn’t entice him, so what did that make her? I had more questions than answers, but one thing was unmistakable; although she released me from her embrace, her hold on me remained.\n\nI was uncertain what this meant for me, but more importantly, I didn’t know what it meant for Chansey. Of all the puzzling things in my head, there remained one clear circumstance; she needed my protection because, for once, I wasn’t the dangerous one.\n\nI lifted my eyes to Chansey’s bedroom window and watched darkness replace the light. She remained standing at her window, believing she was hidden in the darkness, and briefly watched me before she crawled into bed.\n\nShe was lying in her bed, unaware of the strange emotions flooding me. Beings like me didn’t desire romantic relationships with humans, so it was unnatural for me to desire anything other than her blood while all I wanted was to be near her.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/22543.Meredith_Ann_Pierce">About Meredith Ann Pierce</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/22543.Meredith_Ann_Pierce"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1220137936p3/22543.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/22543.Meredith_Ann_Pierce">Meredith Ann Pierce
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
542
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1026400140543319533">Meredith Ann Pierce is a fantasy writer and librarian. Her books deal in fantasy worlds with mythic settings and yet overturn standard expectations, frequently featuring young women who first wish only to love and be loved, yet who must face hazard and danger to save their way of life, their world, and so on, usually without being respected for their efforts until the end of the story.</span>

</div>
</div>
